<div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c <span class=\"icon-newtab\">\n            </a></p>\n        </div>\n\n    <!-- End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" href=\"https://myiopscience.iop.org/signin?origin=a0&return=https%3A%2F%2Fiopscience.iop.org%2Fmyiopscience%2Falerts%2Fsubscribe%3FarticleID%3D0004-637X%2F854%2F2%2F151\"><span\n            class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">0004-637X/854/2/151</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n             <P>The submillimeter galaxy (SMG) HERMES J105751.1+573027 (hereafter HLock01) at <I>z</I>\u00a0=\u00a02.9574\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0001 is one of the brightest gravitationally lensed sources discovered in the <I>Herschel</I> Multi-tiered Extragalactic Survey. Apart from the high flux densities in the far-infrared, it is also extremely bright in the rest-frame ultraviolet (UV), with a total apparent magnitude <I>m</I> <SUB>UV</SUB>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a019.7 mag. We report here deep spectroscopic observations with the Gran Telescopio Canarias of the optically bright lensed images of HLock01. Our results suggest that HLock01 is a merger system composed of the <I>Herschel</I>-selected SMG and an optically bright Lyman break-like galaxy (LBG), separated by only 3.3 kpc in projection. While the SMG appears very massive\u00a0(<I>M</I> <SUB>*</SUB>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a05\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a010<SUP>11</SUP> <I>M</I> <SUB>\u2299</SUB>), with a highly extinguished stellar component (<I>A</I> <SUB> <I>V</I> </SUB>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a04.3 ), the LBG is a young, lower-mass (<I>M</I> <SUB>*</SUB>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a01\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a010<SUP>10</SUP> <I>M</I> <SUB>\u2299</SUB>), but still luminous (<IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$10\\times {L}_{\\mathrm{UV}}^{* }$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/apjaaabb7ieqn1.gif\"></IMG>) satellite galaxy. Detailed analysis of the high signal-to-noise ratio (S/N) rest-frame UV spectrum of the LBG shows complex kinematics of the gas, exhibiting both blueshifted and redshifted absorption components. While the blueshifted component is associated with strong galactic outflows from the massive stars in the LBG, as is common in most star-forming galaxies, the redshifted component may be associated with gas inflow seen along a favorable sightline to the LBG. We also find evidence of an extended gas reservoir around HLock01 at an impact parameter of 110 kpc, through the detection of <span class=\"small-caps\">C ii</span> <I>\u03bb\u03bb</I>1334 absorption in the red wing of a bright Ly<I>\u03b1</I> emitter at <I>z</I>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a03.327. The data presented here highlight the power of gravitational lensing in high S/N studies to probe deeply into the physics of high-<I>z</I> star-forming galaxies.</P> </div>\n    <!-- End abstract bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaaabb7s1\" name=\"apjaaabb7s1\">1.\u00a0Introduction</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>High-<em>z</em> submillimeter galaxies (SMGs) represent a population of the most massive and luminous galaxies in the early universe. They are characterized by dust-enshrouded vigorous star formation, assembling their mass very rapidly over short timescales, the so-called starburst phase (see Blain et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib10\">2002</a>; Casey et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib24\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib24\">2014</a>, for reviews). They are believed to be the progenitors of massive elliptical galaxies predominantly found in clusters of galaxies at lower redshifts (e.g., Daddi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib35\">2009</a>; Capak et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib20\">2011</a>; Walter et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib157\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib157\">2012</a>; Dannerbauer et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib38\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib38\">2014</a>; Riechers et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib123\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib123\">2014</a>; Casey et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib22\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib22\">2015</a>; Oteo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib108\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib108\">2017b</a>), and the study of this population is vital to understand their formation and subsequent evolution.</p><p>Despite the huge progress made over the past decades in understanding the properties of SMGs (e.g., Greve et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib55\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib55\">2005</a>; Magnelli et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib90\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib90\">2012</a>; Riechers et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib122\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib122\">2013</a>; Dowell et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib43\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib43\">2014</a>; Ivison et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib64\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib64\">2016</a>; Micha\u0142owski et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib98\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib98\">2017</a>; Oteo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib107\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib107\">2017a</a>), the main mechanism that drives the intense star formation responsible for the high far-IR luminosities is still a matter of debate (e.g., Swinbank et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib150\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib150\">2008</a>; Gonz\u00e1lez et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib54\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib54\">2011</a>; Micha\u0142owski et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib97\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib97\">2012</a>; Hayward et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib59\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib59\">2013</a>; Narayanan et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib100\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib100\">2015</a>). On one hand, almost all ultraluminous galaxies in the local universe are interacting galaxies and mergers (e.g., Farrah et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib46\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib46\">2001</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib47\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib47\">2002</a>; Bridge et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib13\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib13\">2007</a>; Haan et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib57\">2011</a>). At high-<em>z</em>, a considerable number of SMGs are also found to be galaxy mergers (e.g., Capak et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib19\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib19\">2008</a>; Ivison et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib66\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib66\">2008</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib68\">2013</a>; Tacconi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib154\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib154\">2008</a>; Fu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib48\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib48\">2013</a>; Messias et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib96\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib96\">2014</a>; Rawle et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib117\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib117\">2014</a>; Oteo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib106\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib106\">2016</a>; Riechers et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib125\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib125\">2017</a>; Marrone et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib93\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib93\">2018</a>), although isolated clumpy gas-rich disk galaxies can also reach extremely large SFRs (e.g., Tacconi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib153\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib153\">2010</a>; Bournaud et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib12\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib12\">2014</a>). On the other hand, some authors suggest, based on simulations, that high star formation rates (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn2.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{SFRs}\\,\\gtrapprox \\,1000\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{SFRs}\\,\\gtrapprox \\,1000\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> yr<sup>\u22121</sup>) in some SMGs are difficult to explain by a merger scenario alone, and propose that the predominant mechanism is smooth accretion of cold gas or infall of gas previously ejected via stellar feedback (e.g., Kere\u0161 et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib74\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib74\">2005</a>; Dekel et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib40\">2009</a>; Narayanan et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib100\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib100\">2015</a>).</p><p>Whatever the mechanisms responsible for such extremely large SFRs are, this active phase of SMGs is a clear indication of intense ionizing flux from a young, massive stellar population that dominates the rest-frame ultraviolet (UV). It is thus important to provide detailed characterization of the physical properties of the early episodes of star formation in these galaxies, via spectral diagnostics in the rest-frame UV. However, such studies are limited by the faintness of these galaxies at short wavelengths, with the massive stars giving rise to the UV continuum being embedded in large quantities of dust. Considerable spectroscopic efforts have been successfully used to obtain accurate spectroscopic redshifts, probe for signs of active galactic nucleus (AGN) activity, and investigate properties of the ionized gas in SMGs, mainly by using rest-frame optical nebular emission lines (e.g., Chapman et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib27\">2004</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib26\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib26\">2005</a>; Swinbank et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib152\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib152\">2004</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib151\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib151\">2005</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib149\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib149\">2006</a>; Alaghband-Zadeh et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib1\">2012</a>; Olivares et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib102\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib102\">2016</a>; Casey et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib23\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib23\">2017</a>; Danielson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib37\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib37\">2017</a>). However, the typical faintness of high-<em>z</em> galaxies and the dust obscuration of SMGs make it almost impossible with current facilities to obtain high signal-to-noise ratio (S/N) spectra, a requirement for properly studying the properties of the young stars, and to look for signatures of outflowing/inflowing gas.</p><p>One exception to this principle is the galaxy discussed in this paper, the strong gravitationally lensed SMG HERMES J105751.1+573027 (hereafter HLock01), which is unusually bright in both the optical (<em>R</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a019.7 mag) and in the far-IR (<em>S</em><sub>250 <em>\u03bc</em>m</sub>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a0400 mJy). HLock01 was identified with <em>Herschel</em>/SPIRE in the <em>Herschel</em> Multi-tiered Extragalactic Survey (HerMES; Oliver et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib103\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib103\">2012</a>), and investigated in a series of papers after significant follow-up effort (Conley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib30\">2011</a>; Gavazzi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib50\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib50\">2011</a>; Riechers et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib124\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib124\">2011</a>; Scott et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib135\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib135\">2011</a>; Bussmann et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib15\">2013</a>; Wardlow et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib159\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib159\">2013</a>). Here we give a summary of the main results from those papers. The discovery and its lensing nature were first presented by Conley et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib30\">2011</a>), based on 880 <em>\u03bc</em>m Submillimeter Array (SMA) interferometry and near-IR <em>K</em><sub>p</sub> adaptive optics (AO) observations using NIRC2 on the Keck-II telescope, in which the <em>Herschel</em> source was resolved into four components with a large separation of around 9'' (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f1\">1</a>). Using the Plateau de Bure Interferometer (PdBI), the Combined Array for Research in Millimeter-wave Astronomy (CARMA), and the Green Bank Telescope (GBT), Riechers et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib124\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib124\">2011</a>) and Scott et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib135\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib135\">2011</a>) established the redshift of HLock01 from several CO molecular emission lines as <em>z</em><sub>CO</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9574\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0001. By studying the kinematics of the gas reservoir, Riechers et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib124\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib124\">2011</a>) found a resolved velocity structure in the CO <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn3.gif\" alt=\"$(J=5\\to 4$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">(J=5\\to 4</script></span></span>) emission, similar to what is observed in gas-rich mergers, but the low spatial resolution did not allow a definitive conclusion. The lens modeling was performed by Gavazzi et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib50\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib50\">2011</a>) using NIRC2 <em>K</em><sub>p</sub> and IRAM <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn4.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{CO}\\,(J=5\\to 4$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{CO}\\,(J=5\\to 4</script></span></span>) imaging, as well as deep optical <em>I</em> band imaging with the Subaru Telescope. They showed that the rest-frame UV and optical emission is magnified by a factor of <em>\u03bc</em>\u00a0=\u00a010.9\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.7 by a small group of galaxies at <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a00.6. However, an offset of 2.4 kpc in the source plane was found between the stars that emit at visible/near-IR wavelengths and the gas distribution traced by the molecular gas.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaaabb7f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaaabb7f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0Left panel: <em>g</em>, <em>I</em>, and <em>K</em><sub>s</sub> color image of HLock01 from GTC, Subaru, and WHT, respectively. Dashed lines show the positions of OSIRIS long-slit spectroscopic observations, all centered on the brightest lensed image A, and oriented so as to encompass the other bright lensed images B\u2013D. Right panel: near-IR high-resolution <em>HST</em>/WFC3 F110W image with labeled multiply lensed images at <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a02.95 (blue) and foreground galaxies at <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a00.65 (green). G4 is massive enough to split the lensed image B into two pieces on both sides (B1 and B2, see more details in Gavazzi et al. <a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib50\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib50\">2011</a>). Orange contours show VLA data at 1.4 GHz, and its beam is shown on the bottom right. A spatial offset of the bright lensed images is seen between the short (<em>HST</em> F110W, HLock01-B) and long wavelengths (VLA, HLock01-R). Each image is 16''\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a016'', centered on the brightest lensing galaxy, G1, and oriented such that north is up and east is to the left.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaaabb7f1\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaaabb7f1\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>Later on, Bussmann et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib15\">2013</a>) and Wardlow et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib159\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib159\">2013</a>) presented new imaging data for this system, using <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> (<em>HST</em>) WFC3 F110W, new 880 <em>\u03bc</em>m SMA with higher spatial resolution than the data presented in Conley et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib30\">2011</a>), and Very Large Array (VLA) 1.4 GHz data (at 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />1 resolution). The new images show the same spatial offsets of the bright lensed images seen between the short and long wavelengths (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f1\">1</a>), noticed by Conley et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib30\">2011</a>) and Gavazzi et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib50\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib50\">2011</a>). A new lens model was determined by Bussmann et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib15\">2013</a>) using the SMA 880 <em>\u03bc</em>m data, showing a large dust distribution, magnified by 9.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.4 with an effective radius of 4 kpc in the source plane. Its centroid matches the position of the gas distribution traced by the molecular gas, which we attribute to the source of the luminous far-IR emission, but both are offset with respect to the stars that are seen in the visible/near-IR (UV/optical in the rest-frame). Finally, Rigopoulou et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib128\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib128\">2018</a>) discuss the applicability of the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]88/[N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]122 line ratio as a metallicity indicator in high-redshift submillimeter luminous galaxies and found that the gas metallicity of HLock01 is 0.6\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>Z</em><sub>gas</sub>/<em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub>\u00a0&lt;\u00a01.0.</p><p>Due to the high dust content of HLock01, one could expect that its rest-frame UV and optical light are heavily obscured by dust, as in most SMGs. However, HLock01 is unusually bright in its rest-frame UV, and their colors are also consistent with those of <em>z</em>\u00a0~\u00a03 Lyman break galaxies (LBGs; Steidel et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib147\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib147\">1996</a>) with (<em>G</em>\u2013<em>R</em>)\u00a0=0.5 and (<em>U</em>\u2013<em>G</em>)\u00a0=\u00a01.4. In this paper, we present a detailed analysis of the optically bright lensed images of HLock01, based on deep spectroscopic observations with the 10.4 m Gran Telescopio Canarias (GTC). Throughout the paper we adopt the name \"HLock01-B\" for the optically bright LBG-like galaxy, and \"HLock01-R\" for the <em>Herschel</em>-selected SMG (where \"B\" and \"R\" stand for blue and red galaxies, respectively). Thanks to the large collecting area of the GTC, to the lensing magnification of the source, and to the small obscuration toward HLock01-B, we can perform a detailed analysis of its physical properties.</p><p>The paper is organized as follows. In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s2\">2</a>, we describe our spectroscopic and imaging observations. Our analysis of the rest-frame UV spectrum of HLock01-B is presented in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s3\">3</a>. The main properties of both components of HLock01, derived from SED fitting, are discussed in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s4\">4</a>. Finally, in Sections <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s5\">5</a> and <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s6\">6</a>, we discus our results and summarize our main findings. A concordance cosmology with matter and dark energy density \u03a9<sub>m</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.3, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.7, and Hubble constant <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=70 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup> are assumed throughout this work. All magnitudes are given in the AB system.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaaabb7s2\" name=\"apjaaabb7s2\">2.\u00a0Observations</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjaaabb7s2-1\" name=\"apjaaabb7s2-1\">2.1.\u00a0GTC/OSIRIS Spectroscopic and Imaging Observations</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Rest-frame UV spectroscopic observations were obtained with the Optical System for Imaging and low-Intermediate-Resolution Integrated Spectroscopy instrument (OSIRIS<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7fn1\">17</a></sup>\n) on the 10.4 m GTC. The data used in this paper were obtained in service mode over seven different nights, between 2015 April 26 and June 21 in dark and gray Moon conditions as part of the GTC program GTCMULTIPLE2A-15A (PI: R. Marques-Chaves). We used the R2500V and R2500R grisms, with dispersions of 0.80 and 1.04 \u00c5 px<sup>\u22121</sup>, respectively. These two grisms provide a full spectral coverage of 4500\u20137700 \u00c5, which corresponds to 1150\u20131950 \u00c5 in the rest-frame at <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a02.95. The OSIRIS 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />2-wide slit was centered on the brightest lensed image of HLock01-B (image A), and oriented so as to encompass the other lensed images B, C, and D, at sky positions angles (PA) of \u221239<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />4, \u221282<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />9, and 44<sup>\u25e6</sup>, respectively (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f1\">1</a>, left panel). Given this configuration, the corresponding instrumental resolution for the R2500V and R2500R grisms is <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />180 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>. In total, 15 exposures of 900 s were acquired with each grism, equally split between different PAs. A summary of the rest-frame UV spectroscopic observations of HLock01-B used in this work is shown in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7t1\">1</a>.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaaabb7t1\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 1.</b>\u00a0\nOSIRIS Spectroscopic Observations of HLock01-B\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaaabb7t1\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/suppdata/apjaaabb7t1_lr.gif\" align=\"center\">dark</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/suppdata/apjaaabb7t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aaabb7\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/suppdata/apjaaabb7t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>The data were processed with standard <span class=\"small-caps\">Iraf</span><sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7fn2\">18</a></sup>\n and <span class=\"small-caps\">Python</span> tasks. Each individual two-dimensional spectrum was bias-subtracted and flat-field corrected. The wavelength calibration was done for every observing night using HgAr+Ne+Xe arc lamps. Finally, individual 2D spectra were background subtracted. The 1D spectra were then extracted and corrected for the instrumental response using observations of the standard stars Ross 640 and GD 153.</p><p>We also obtained spectra of the galaxies in the group responsible for the gravitational lensing of HLock01, with two additional long-slit spectra to encompass G1\u2013G4, and G3\u2013G5, respectively. For this, we used a lower spectral resolution grism, R1000R, which provides a wider spectral range (5100\u201310000 \u00c5), which with a 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />2-wide slit gives a spectral resolution of <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />400 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>. The other lensing galaxies, G2 and G6, are covered by the long-slit spectra discussed before to study the lensed images of HLock01-B. For the galaxies G1 and G2, we detect several absorption lines (e.g., K and H of Ca <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3934,3969, H<sub><em>\u03b4</em></sub> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>4102, and Mgb\u00a0<em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>5176), as well as a prominent Balmer break at redshift <em>z</em><sub>G1</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.6464\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0007, and <em>z</em><sub>G2</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.6492\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0009, respectively. The spectra of G3, G4, and G5 are too noisy for a reliable measurement of their redshifts, but we marginally detect a jump at 6500\u20136600 \u00c5, compatible with a Balmer break at <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a00.65. Thus it appears that these galaxies belong to a group at <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a00.65, slightly larger than the previously assumed redshift (<em>z</em><sub>phot</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.6\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04; Oyaizu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib109\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib109\">2008</a>). For the brightest member of the group, G1, we measured a large velocity dispersion <em>\u03c3</em>\u00a0=\u00a0(438\u00a0\u00b1\u00a030) km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, in agreement with the velocity dispersion of the deflector found in the lens model presented in Gavazzi et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib50\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib50\">2011</a>), indicating that the background sources are lensed by a galaxy group-scale dark matter halo.</p><p>Additionally, broadband imaging with the Sloan <em>g</em>' filter was obtained with OSIRIS on 2017 January 24, as part of the GTC program GTCMULTIPLE3A-16B (PI: I. P\u00e9rez-Fournon). The total exposure time was 2160 s, split into 12 individual exposures of 180 s each. Each frame was reduced individually following standard reduction procedures in <span class=\"small-caps\">Iraf</span>. The registration and combination were done using <span class=\"small-caps\">Scamp</span> (Bertin <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib7\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib7\">2006</a>) and <span class=\"small-caps\">Swarp</span> (Bertin <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib8\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib8\">2010</a>). The seeing of the final image is <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />8 (full width at half maximum, FWHM).</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaaabb7s2-2\" name=\"apjaaabb7s2-2\">2.2.\u00a0William Herschel Telescope (WHT)/LIRIS Near-IR Imaging</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Near-IR broadband imaging was obtained on 2011 March 22 in the <em>K</em><sub>s</sub> filter (PI: I. P\u00e9rez-Fournon), using the Long-slit Intermediate Resolution Infrared Spectrograph instrument (LIRIS) mounted at the WHT. LIRIS has a field of view of 4<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcm.gif\" alt=\"farcm\" align=\"baseline\" />27\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a04<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcm.gif\" alt=\"farcm\" align=\"baseline\" />27 with a plate scale of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />25 pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>. The total integration time was 60 minutes, spit into 180 individual exposures of 20 s, adopting a random dither pattern in 15 different positions. The data reduction was carried out using the IAC's <span class=\"small-caps\">Iraf lirisdr</span><sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7fn3\">19</a></sup>\n task. The seeing of the final image was 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />63 FWHM. The astrometric and flux calibrations were performed using 2MASS stars in the field.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaaabb7s2-3\" name=\"apjaaabb7s2-3\">2.3.\u00a0Ancillary Data</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Additional data used in this work consist of a combination of shallow and deep images. Archival <em>U</em> and <em>R</em> wide-field images and catalogs from MEGACAM on the Canada\u2013France\u2013Hawaii Telescope (CFHT), processed and stacked using the MegaPipe image staking pipeline (Gwyn <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib56\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib56\">2008</a>), were downloaded from the Canadian Astronomy Data Centre (CADC<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7fn4\">20</a></sup>\n). Total exposure times are 4200 and 3300 s in <em>U</em> and <em>R</em> bands, with an average seeing of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />83 and 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />73 FWHM, respectively. HLock01 was also imaged with WFC3 on <em>HST</em> under the snapshot program 12488 (PI: Negrello). The source was observed in the broadband filter F110W with a total exposure time of 276.1 s. The <em>HST</em> imaging was initially presented in Bussmann et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib15\">2013</a>) and Wardlow et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib159\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib159\">2013</a>). <em>Spitzer</em>/IRAC images and catalogs in the 3.6 and 4.5 <em>\u03bc</em>m bands from the <em>Spitzer</em> Extragalactic Representative Volume Survey (SERVS; Mauduit et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib95\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib95\">2012</a>) were obtained from the IRSA archive.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7fn5\">21</a></sup>\n We also used the IRAC and MIPS imaging from the <em>Spitzer</em> Wide-Area InfraRed Extragalactic survey data (SWIRE; Lonsdale et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib82\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib82\">2003</a>).</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaaabb7s3\" name=\"apjaaabb7s3\">3.\u00a0Rest-frame UV Spectrum of HLock01-B</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>As in other star-forming galaxies, the rest-frame UV spectrum of HLock01-B is characterized by the integrated light from the hot young stellar population with superimposed resonant strong absorption lines produced by the interstellar medium (ISM) and stellar winds. These spectral features can provide detailed information on dynamical, physical, and chemical properties of the atomic and ionized gas in the galaxy, as well as insights on the properties of the young OB stars responsible for the bright continuum (e.g., Pettini et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib114\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib114\">2000</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib113\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib113\">2002</a>; Shapley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib138\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib138\">2003</a>; Jones et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib72\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib72\">2012</a>; Steidel et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib148\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib148\">2016</a>; Rigby et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib126\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib126\">2017a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib127\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib127\">2017b</a>). Large-scale outflows of interstellar gas, resulting from the kinetic energy deposited by the star formation activity, are a common feature in these galaxies (e.g., Shapley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib138\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib138\">2003</a>; Steidel et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib146\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib146\">2010</a>).</p><p>Despite the differences in the S/N of the spectra of the different lensed images, there are no differences in the profiles of the absorption features and no evidence for velocity offsets between them, as expected. Spectra of the lensed images B and D show redder UV slopes (<em>\u03b2</em>), likely due to differential extinction from the proximity of their light path to the foreground galaxies. Thus we will focus our rest-frame UV analysis on the spectrum of the lensed image A, which has higher S/N (~20\u201340, depending on the wavelength range) and is less affected by absorption in the ISM of the foreground galaxies.</p><p>The rest-frame UV spectrum of the lensed image A of HLock01-B, shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f2\">2</a>, is remarkably similar to the <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a03 LBG composite spectrum (Shapley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib138\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib138\">2003</a>). It shows a damped Ly<em>\u03b1</em> absorption line, and a series of strong absorption lines associated with either stellar winds from massive stars (e.g., C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1548,1550) or ISM lines of several species. However, there are significant differences between the expected wavelengths and velocities (\u0394<em>v</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a0500 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>) of the ISM in the <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a03 template (in orange in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f2\">2</a>) and in our spectrum (discussed in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s3-2\">3.2</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaaabb7f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaaabb7f2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f2_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 2.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f2_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 2.</strong>\u00a0Combined GTC/OSIRIS rest-frame UV spectrum of the lensed image A of HLock01-B. Vertical dotted lines identify the best defined photospheric absorption lines used to derive the systemic redshift of HLock01-B (<em>z</em><sub>sys</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9546\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0004). Strong absorption lines associated with interstellar gas and stellar winds are marked with vertical dashed lines. The C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii]</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1906,1908 nebular emission doublet and fine-structure emission lines of Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> are marked with dash-dotted lines. For comparison, we show in orange the <em>z</em>\u00a0~\u00a03 LBG subset composite with the damped Ly<em>\u03b1</em> profile from Shapley et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib138\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib138\">2003</a>) at the systemic redshift of HLock01-B (downshifted for clarity). The wavelength windows of four metallicity indices (e.g., F1370, etc.), used to derive the metallicity of young stars in HLock01-B, are also marked. Short vertical blue and green lines mark the positions of absorption lines of intervening systems at <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a01.458 and <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a02.189, respectively. The sky emission is also plotted in red, showing the locations of strong sky emission lines.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaaabb7f2\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaaabb7f2\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The OSIRIS spectrum also shows several narrow absorption lines produced by intervening systems at lower redshifts along the line of sight to HLock01-B. We identify at least two intervening metal systems at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.4583\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0008, and <em>z</em>\u00a0= 2.1889\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0007. Some of these absorption lines may contaminate the profiles of lines of HLock01-B, and hence they are taken into account in our analysis (in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s3-2\">3.2</a>).</p><p>In addition, three strong Ly<em>\u03b1</em> lines at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.72, 3.15, and 3.27 were serendipitously detected in two of our GTC long-slit spectra (see Appendix <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7app1\">A</a>). In particular, the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> line at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.27 is associated with an Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emitting galaxy at 14'' SW from the lensing galaxy G1, and shows an unusual absorption line in its red-emission wing consistent with C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1334 at the redshift of HLock01-R (<em>z</em><sub>CO</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9574; Riechers et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib124\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib124\">2011</a>; Scott et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib135\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib135\">2011</a>). We discuss this absorption feature in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s5-3\">5.3</a>.</p><h3 id=\"apjaaabb7s3-1\" name=\"apjaaabb7s3-1\">3.1.\u00a0Systemic Redshift of HLock01-B</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Stellar photospheric features are formed in the photospheres of hot stars, and although much weaker than the ISM lines, they can provide a measurement of the systemic redshift of the galaxy. Within the wavelength range covered by our data, we identified several photospheric absorption features (marked with dotted lines in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f2\">2</a>), but some of them are blends from multiple transitions. Using the cleanest among these, listed in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7t2\">2</a>, we derive the mean redshift of the stars to be <em>z</em><sub>stars</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9546\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0004.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaaabb7t2\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 2.</b>\u00a0\nStellar rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">1718.55</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">6796.37</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" wavelengths.\n<a name=\"apjaaabb7t1fnb\" id=\"apjaaabb7t1fnb\"></a><sup> b</sup>Values measured from the centroid for the individual photospheric line.\n<a name=\"apjaaabb7t1fnc\" id=\"apjaaabb7t1fnc\"></a><sup> c</sup>Value refers to the blended C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> and N\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span> photospheric lines.\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/suppdata/apjaaabb7t2_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aaabb7\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/suppdata/apjaaabb7t2_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>The nebular C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii]</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1906,1908 emission is weakly detected (3<em>\u03c3</em>) at <em>z</em><sub>C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.954\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.002, in agreement with <em>z</em><sub>stars</sub>, but the doublet is not resolved in our spectrum, and the existing data are too noisy for a reliable measurement of this feature. Therefore throughout the paper we adopt the redshift of stellar photospheric lines as the systemic redshift of HLock01-B, <em>z</em><sub>sys</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9546\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0004.</p><p>The difference of \u0394<em>v</em>\u00a0=\u00a0210 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> between the systemic redshift of HLock01-B <em>z</em><sub>sys</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9546, and the redshift of HLock01-R from the molecular gas lines <em>z</em><sub>CO</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9574 (Riechers et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib124\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib124\">2011</a>; Scott et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib135\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib135\">2011</a>), cannot be explained by errors in redshift measurements. The velocity offset derived here and the complex dynamical structure of the molecular gas reservoir discussed in Riechers et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib124\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib124\">2011</a>) suggest that HLock01-B is a separate galaxy, different from the <em>Herschel</em> SMG (HLock01-R), but both forming a close merger. Nevertheless, similar velocity offsets, interpreted as rotational velocities in some cases, have been found in a few massive galaxies at high-<em>z</em> (e.g., Law et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib77\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib77\">2012</a>; Jim\u00e9nez-Andrade et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib70\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib70\">2017</a>; Toft et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib155\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib155\">2017</a>). A more detailed discussion is presented in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s5-1\">5.1</a>.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaaabb7s3-2\" name=\"apjaaabb7s3-2\">3.2.\u00a0Kinematics of the ISM</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Within our spectral range, we identify 11 strong absorption features, including low-ionization lines (Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1260, O <span class=\"small-caps\">i</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1302, Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1304, C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1334, Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1526, Fe <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1608, and Al <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1670), and high-ionization lines associated with a hot gas phase (Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn5.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda \\lambda $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda \\lambda</script></span></span> 1393,1402, and C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1548,1550). In low-ionization lines, the interstellar component usually dominates over the stellar contribution, and thus they are useful for studying the kinematics of the ISM (Shapley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib138\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib138\">2003</a>; Steidel et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib146\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib146\">2010</a>). High-ionization lines are associated with strong winds from young stars, and predominantly trace gas at higher temperatures (<em>T</em>\u00a0\u2265\u00a010<sup>4</sup> K).</p><p>For the kinematic analysis of the ISM, we first normalized the GTC/OSIRIS spectrum of HLock01-B using the pseudo-continuum windows that are free of absorption and emission features identified by Rix et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib129\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib129\">2004</a>).</p><p>Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f3\">3</a> shows the normalized profiles of the strongest absorption lines seen in our spectrum. We note that all ISM lines present an unusual velocity profile with the maximum optical depth located at a mean <em>v</em>\u00a0=\u00a0(+370\u00a0\u00b1\u00a030) km s<sup>\u22121</sup> relative to the stars of HLock01-B, or <em>v</em>\u00a0=\u00a0(+170\u00a0\u00b1\u00a030) km s<sup>\u22121</sup> relative to the <em>Herschel</em> SMG at <em>z</em><sub>CO</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9574. This can be understood as gas apparently moving toward the young stars, since all the interstellar lines are seen against the UV stellar continuum. This absorption is strong in the low-ionization lines (the first three columns in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f3\">3</a>), likely with saturated profiles,<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7fn6\">22</a></sup>\n but it is also present, although notably weaker in high-ionization ones, like C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> and Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> (the last two columns in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f3\">3</a>). The spectrum of HLock01-B also shows a secondary but broader absorption component centered at a mean <em>v</em>\u00a0=\u00a0(\u2212220\u00a0\u00b1\u00a060) km s<sup>\u22121</sup> relative to its systemic redshift, which is a characteristic of large-scale outflows of material in HLock01-B. This blueshifted component is stronger in high-ionization lines than in low-ionization ones (it is detected in C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1334, Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1260, and Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1526, but is not clear in O <span class=\"small-caps\">i</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1302, Fe <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1608 or Al <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span><em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1670), suggesting that the outflowing gas is mostly ionized, or the neutral gas has a lower covering factor than the ionized gas.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaaabb7f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaaabb7f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f3_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0Normalized profiles of low- (first three columns) and high-ionization (last two columns) absorption lines associated with the ISM and stellar winds, respectively. The <em>x</em> axis is the velocity (in km s<sup>\u22121</sup>) relative to the stars of HLock01-B, <em>z</em><sub>sys</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9546, and the <em>y</em> axis is the normalized flux. Almost all ISM and wind lines present an unusual velocity profile, with two distinct absorption components on either side of systemic velocity (negative and positive velocities shaded in blue and red, respectively, for visual purpose only). The absorption component with the maximum intensity is located at <em>v</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a0+370 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> (shaded in red). Another broader component is also detected in high-ionization lines, like C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn6.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda \\lambda $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda \\lambda</script></span></span>1548,1550 and Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1393,1402, and in some ISM lines (shaded in blue). Dotted lines indicate spectral features in HLock01 other than those to which the label in each plot refers. Short vertical blue and green solid lines mark the expected positions of absorption lines from intervening metal systems at lower redshift.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaaabb7f3\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaaabb7f3\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The absorption profiles resulting from these two components extend over a velocity range \u0394\u00a0<em>v</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a01700 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, from ~\u22121000 to ~+700 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, much larger than in other high-<em>z</em> lensed LBGs (Pettini et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib114\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib114\">2000</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib113\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib113\">2002</a>; Cabanac et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib16\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib16\">2008</a>; Quider et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib115\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib115\">2009</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib116\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib116\">2010</a>; Dessauges-Zavadsky et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib42\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib42\">2010</a>). The C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> doublet is even broader than the ISM lines, with \u0394<em>v</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a03000 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, indicative of a strong contribution from winds due to radiation pressure of the most massive and luminous stars of HLock01-B. The velocity profile of the C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> doublet shows a strong P-Cygni profile, with the red-emission wing being attenuated by the two narrow, redshifted (<em>v</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a0+370 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>) interstellar absorption components of C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>.</p><p>In order to understand the blueshifed and redshifted ISM absorption components, we simultaneously fit two Gaussians to the low- and high-ionization lines. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f4\">4</a> shows an example of our fit to the low-ionization C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1334, and high-ionization Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1393 lines, and Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7t3\">3</a> summarizes the results for all strong absorption lines, except the ones that are affected by the proximity of other lines (<span class=\"small-caps\">O i</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1302, Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1304, and Fe <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1608). In C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1548,1550 we only fit the redshifted component, as the blueshifted one is affected by strong winds.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaaabb7f4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaaabb7f4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f4_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 4.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f4_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 4.</strong>\u00a0Example of the double-Gaussian fit of the low- (C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1334) and high-ionization lines (Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1393). Lower and upper <em>x</em> axes are the velocity (in km s<sup>\u22121</sup>) relative to the stars of the LBG (HLock01-B) and to the molecular gas of the SMG (HLock01-R), respectively. The <em>y</em> axis is the normalized flux. The redshifted (red color) and blueshifted (blue color) components represent outflowing and inflowing gas along the line of sight of HLock01-B, respectively. The sum of the two components is also shown in gray. Black dashed and green dotted\u2013dashed vertical lines mark the zero velocity position with respect to <em>z</em><sub>sys</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9546 (HLock01-B) and <em>z</em><sub>CO</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9574 (HLock01-R), respectively.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary align=\"center\">&lt;180</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<p><strong>Note.</strong> Columns are as follows: (1) and (2) ion and the corresponding vacuum wavelength; (3) velocity range for the measurements of the total rest-frame equivalent width (blueshifted and redshifted components); (4) total rest-frame equivalent width and 1<em>\u03c3</em> error; (5)\u2013(7) redshift, rest-frame equivalent width, and full width half maximum (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn8.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{FWHM}=2\\sqrt{2\\mathrm{ln}2}\\sigma $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{FWHM}=2\\sqrt{2\\mathrm{ln}2}\\sigma</script></span></span>) of the blueshifted absorption component from the Gaussian fit; (8)\u2013(10) are the same as (5)\u2013(7), but in this case applied to the redshifted absorption component from the Gaussian fit.</p>\n<a name=\"apjaaabb7t2fna\" id=\"apjaaabb7t2fna\"></a><sup> a</sup>The profile of Fe <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1608 is affected by other absorption lines from an intervening system at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.4583\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0005.\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/suppdata/apjaaabb7t3_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aaabb7\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/suppdata/apjaaabb7t3_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>The fitted blueshifted component (blue dashed lines in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f4\">4</a>) has its peak located at <em>z</em><sub>blue</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9519\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0009 (or <em>v</em><sub>blue</sub>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" /> \u2212220 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> relative to the systemic redshift of HLock01-B), and shows a broad profile (FWHM\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a0900 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, after accounting for the instrumental broadening) extended over a velocity range from about \u22121000 to +600\u00a0km\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>. Despite the fact that a potentially large contribution from stellar winds may be present in the high-ionization lines, for the low-ionization ones, this effect is negligible. Thus the broadness of the blueshifted component in the low-ionization line C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> (as well as in others like Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1260 and Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1526; see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f3\">3</a>) suggests highly turbulent kinematics of the outflowing gas. As a comparison, the velocity profile of the low-ionization interstellar lines in the <em>z</em>\u00a0~\u00a03 LBGs composite spectrum of Shapley et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib138\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib138\">2003</a>) shows an average FWHM\u00a0=\u00a0(560\u00a0\u00b1\u00a0150) km s<sup>\u22121</sup>. Despite the broadness of the outflowing low-ionization lines in HLock01-B, they show smaller rest-frame equivalent widths (by a factor of two) than in typical LBGs.</p><p>The fitted redshifted component (red dashed line in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f4\">4</a>) has its peak located at <em>z</em><sub>red</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9596\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0003, and shows a narrow profile (FWHM\u00a0=\u00a0310 and 104 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, for C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> and Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>, respectively). If dynamically related to HLock01, its positive velocity relatively to both HLock01-B (<em>v</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a0+370 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>) and HLock01-R (<em>v</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a0+170 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>) is indicative of gas moving toward the system. This narrower component is seen in all absorption lines, but appears almost unresolved in the high-ionization ones, suggesting that these lines are dominated by the interstellar component. Moreover, the differences in the FWHM between the redshifted component in low- and high-ionization lines (see Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7t3\">3</a>) also suggests that cold and warm gas may have different kinematics and origins. A clearer picture of the origin of this redshifted component of the ISM may come from deeper and higher spectral resolution observations. In particular, fully resolved ISM components of HLock01-B with unsaturated profiles may be used to derive chemical abundances, using the apparent optical depth method, as has been done in other studies of strongly lensed star-forming galaxies (e.g., Pettini et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib113\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib113\">2002</a>; Quider et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib115\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib115\">2009</a>; Dessauges-Zavadsky et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib42\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib42\">2010</a>).</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaaabb7s3-3\" name=\"apjaaabb7s3-3\">3.3.\u00a0Stellar Metallicity and Age of HLock01-B</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Leitherer et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib79\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib79\">2001</a>), Rix et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib129\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib129\">2004</a>), and later on Sommariva et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib143\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib143\">2012</a>) showed that several blends of stellar UV photospheric absorption lines can be used to trace the metallicity of young stars, by measuring equivalent widths of these blends in specific wavelength windows. These metallicity indicators have been successfully applied in several works (e.g., Quider et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib115\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib115\">2009</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib116\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib116\">2010</a>; Patr\u00edcio et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib110\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib110\">2016</a>), using high S/N spectra due to the faintness of these absorption lines. They are defined as the F1370, F1425, F1460, F1501, and F1978 indices, and their wavelength windows are shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f2\">2</a> (except for the latter one which is not covered by our data).</p><p>We measured the equivalent widths of the features in each of these spectral windows using our normalized spectrum. We then applied the calibrations of Sommariva et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib143\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib143\">2012</a>) to obtain the corresponding metallicity. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7t4\">4</a> summarizes our measurements. All indices agree in a sub-solar metallicity, and we use the mean value to derive the metallicity of the UV stars in HLock01-B as <em>Z</em><sub>stars</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0(0.4\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1)<em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub>.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaaabb7t4\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 4.</b>\u00a0\nMetallicity Estimates Following Sommariva et al.
