xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn16.gif\" alt=\"${2.76}_{-0.85}^{+1.22}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{2.76}_{-0.85}^{+1.22}</script></span></span>\n</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Gyr<sup>\u22121</sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\"><em>Z</em></td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">0.4\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">0.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\"><em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub></td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/suppdata/apjaaabb7t5_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aaabb7\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/suppdata/apjaaabb7t5_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>The strength of any P-Cygni features formed in the expanding winds of the most massive stars is also sensitive to the metallicity, along with the age and the initial mass function (IMF) of the stellar population. In order to study the P-Cygni stellar wind features in HLock01-B, we use model spectra computed with the spectral synthesis code <span class=\"small-caps\">Starburst99</span> (Leitherer et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib80\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib80\">1999</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib79\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib79\">2001</a>) and perform <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> minimization to our normalized data. In generating the <span class=\"small-caps\">Starburst99</span> spectra, we assumed both continuous and instantaneous star formation scenarios. We adopt a Salpeter slope for the IMF between 1 and 100\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>, and ages ranging from 1 to 100\u00a0Myr. <span class=\"small-caps\">Starburst99</span> models were generated using libraries of empirical UV spectra from Large and Small Magallenic Cloud stars (LMC/SMC, which correspond to a metallicity <em>Z</em><sub>MC</sub>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a00.4  <em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub>) and Galactic stars (<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />1 <em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub>).</p><p>Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f5\">5</a> shows two high-ionization lines associated with stellar winds used in this fit: N\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">v</span>\u00a0<em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1238,1242 (left panels) and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>\u00a0<em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1548,1550 (middle panels). <span class=\"small-caps\">Starburst99</span> models are plotted for continuous (upper panels) and instantaneous (lower panels) star formation scenarios. We excluded in the fit the region encompassing the interstellar absorption in C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>, between 1543 and 1553 \u00c5, which is not associated with the stellar P-Cygni profile.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaaabb7f5\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaaabb7f5\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f5_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 5.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 5.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f5_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 5.</strong>\u00a0Comparison of the normalized spectrum of HLock01-B (black solid lines) with empirical models from <span class=\"small-caps\">Starburst99</span> for high-ionization lines associated with stellar winds: N\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">v</span>\u00a0<em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1238,1242 (left panels) and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>\u00a0<em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1548,1550 (middle panels). Upper panels show models for continuous star formation with a stellar population age <em>t</em>\u00a0=\u00a0100 Myr, and for metallicities of 0.4  <em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub> (LMC/SMG stars, blue solid lines) and 1  <em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub> (Galactic stars, red solid lines). Lower panels show the comparison of the spectrum of HLock01-B with models for an instantaneous burst with <em>Z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.4  <em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub> and ages of 4 (blue), 6 (green), and 15 (red) Myr. The wavelength windows used to perform the <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> minimization are marked in gray. Note that we exclude in this fit the region of strong interstellar absorption in C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> (between 1543 and 1553). The right panel shows the <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> (<em>N</em><sub>dof</sub>\u00a0=\u00a038) as a function of the age of the stellar population for continuous and instantaneous star formation models, and metallicities of 0.4  <em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub> and 1  <em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub>, as indicated. A good fit is seen for models using LMC/SMG stars (0.4  <em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub>) with around 6 Myr old burst.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaaabb7f5\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f5\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaaabb7f5\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f5\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> (<em>N</em><sub>dof</sub>\u00a0=\u00a038) as a function of the age of the stellar population for all models is shown in the right panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f5\">5</a>. The model using LMC/SMG stars (0.4  <em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub>) with a ~6 Myr old burst matches the data better (<em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup>/<em>N</em><sub>dof</sub>\u00a0=\u00a039/38), reproducing quite well both the line profiles of N\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">v</span> and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>, in particular the regions of the blueshifted absorption wind component of the <span class=\"small-caps\">C</span> <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> P-Cygni profile and its red-emission wing (regions of 1536 to 1542 and 1554 to 1563 \u00c5, respectively). Bursts over slightly longer periods (<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/lesssim.gif\" alt=\"lesssim\" align=\"baseline\" />25 Myr) can also recover the stellar blueshifted absorption of <span class=\"small-caps\">C</span> <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>, but fail to reproduce the red-emission wing of HLock01-B (see the lower panels of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f5\">5</a> for an example of a 15-Myr-old burst). However, our results should be treated with care, given the assumptions made on the slope and upper end cut-off of the IMF. Moreover, the P-Cygni profile of N\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">v</span>\u00a0<em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1238,1242 could also be affected by the red wing of the damped Ly<em>\u03b1</em> absorption line (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s3-4\">3.4</a>).</p><p>All methods used in this work to derive the metallicity of the young stars in HLock01-B point to a <em>Z</em><sub>stars</sub>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a00.4<em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub> value. Our metallicity measurements are slightly different from the measurement of gas metallicity in HLock01-R (0.6\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>Z</em><sub>gas</sub>/<em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub>\u00a0&lt;\u00a01.0) by Rigopoulou et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib128\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib128\">2018</a>), using the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]88/[N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]122 line ratio as a metallicity indicator. This provides additional evidence that the bright <em>Herschel</em> SMG (HLock01-R) and the bright LBG-like galaxy (HLock01-B) are likely different galaxies with distinct enrichment histories.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaaabb7s3-4\" name=\"apjaaabb7s3-4\">3.4.\u00a0The Damped Ly<em>\u03b1</em> Profile</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The Ly<em>\u03b1</em> line in the spectrum of HLock01-B shows a strong damped Ly<em>\u03b1</em> profile, with the minimum lying in the range from <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />4809 to 4815 \u00c5 (or <em>v</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a0+100 to +500 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> relative to <em>z</em><sub>sys;</sub> see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f6\">6</a>). We used the software <span class=\"small-caps\">PyAstronomy</span><sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7fn7\">23</a></sup>\n to generate theoretical Voigt profiles and perform <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> minimization to the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> profile. However, we noted differences in the absorption profile in the blue and red damping wings, with the absorption being more pronounced in the latter. The blue wing is more noisy and less constrained than the red one, likely due to additional absorption from the intergalactic medium in the line of sight toward HLock01-B. The red wing is well fitted with a neutral hydrogen column density <em>N</em>(H <span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>)\u00a0=\u00a0(5.83\u00a0\u00b1\u00a01.24)\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a010<sup>20</sup> cm<sup>\u22122</sup> centered at <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />4813 \u00c5 or <em>v</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a0+370 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> with respect to <em>z</em><sub>sys</sub>. Therefore we interpret that most of the damped absorption is due to the redshifted component of the ISM seen in the spectrum of HLock01-B, which consists primarily of neutral gas and presents a large optical depth. Our derived column density of H <span class=\"small-caps\">i</span> is in the range of typical values measured in other lensed galaxies (e.g., Pettini et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib114\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib114\">2000</a>; Cabanac et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib16\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib16\">2008</a>; Dessauges-Zavadsky et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib42\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib42\">2010</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaaabb7f6\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaaabb7f6\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f6_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 6.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 6.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f6_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 6.</strong>\u00a0Portion of the spectrum of HLock01-B encompassing the region of the Ly<em>\u03b1</em> absorption line. The <em>x</em> axis is the observed wavelength (in \u00c5) and the <em>y</em> axis is the normalized intensity. Overlaid is the best Voigt profile fit (red solid line) for <em>N</em>(H <span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>)\u00a0=\u00a0(5.83\u00a0\u00b1\u00a01.24)\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a010<sup>20</sup> cm<sup>\u22122</sup> centered at <em>z</em><sub>Ly<em>\u03b1</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.9594, as well as the 1<em>\u03c3</em> error (red filled area).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaaabb7f6\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f6\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaaabb7f6\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f6\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h3 id=\"apjaaabb7s3-5\" name=\"apjaaabb7s3-5\">3.5.\u00a0Weak Emission Lines</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>As discussed in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s3-1\">3.1</a>, the nebular C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii]</span>\u00a0<em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1906,1908 emission is barely detected in our OSIRIS spectrum, and the doublet is not resolved. Despite the low significance of the detection (3<em>\u03c3</em>), we fit a Gaussian to the unresolved C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii]</span> doublet. We derive <em>z</em><sub>C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.954\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.002 and EW<sub>0</sub><sup>C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]</sup>\u00a0=\u00a0(1.0\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.3) \u00c5. Other semiforbidden transitions often detected in the spectra of star-forming galaxies are the O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii]</span>\u00a0<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn17.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda \\lambda $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda \\lambda</script></span></span>1661,1666 lines, but these are not detected in our spectrum, despite the high continuum S/N in this spectral region (around 25). The absence of these nebular lines in HLock01-B may be due to their faintness or to contamination with the overlapping blueshifted component of the Al\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1670 interstellar line. In addition to C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii]</span>, we also detect emission features from the excited fine-structure transitions Si\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii*</span>\u00a0<em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1264, 1309, and 1533. Their profiles appear slightly asymmetric (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f2\">2</a>), with the centroids redshifted with respect to <em>z</em><sub>sys</sub> by a mean of <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />+120\u00a0\u00b1\u00a050 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>. This velocity offset may be due to the neighboring red component of resonance absorption features (Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1260, O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>\u00a0+Si\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>\u00a0<em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1303, and Si\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>\u00a0<em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1526), which attenuate the blue edges of the fine-structure emission profiles. We measure rest-frame equivalent widths of 0.32\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.06, 0.22\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.09, and 0.26\u00a0\u00b10.14 \u00c5 for Si\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii*</span>\u00a0<em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>1264,1309, and 1533, respectively.</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaaabb7s4\" name=\"apjaaabb7s4\">4.\u00a0Physical Properties from the Spectral Energy Distribution</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Conley et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib30\">2011</a>) analyzed the SED of HLock01, considering only a single lensed background source. They simultaneously fitted the emission in the optical/near-IR with longer wavelength data (far-IR and submm), but the fit did not explain the IRAC fluxes and overestimated the <em>K</em><sub>p</sub> and MIPS 70 <em>\u03bc</em>m flux densities by a factor of 2 or more. We now know that HLock01 is composed of two different, spatially and spectrally offset sources, and thus the energy balance method (between dust-absorbed stellar continuum and the reprocessed dust emission in the far-IR), which was previously invoked, cannot be applied to the integrated photometry by considering a single source.</p><p>From a revised photometric analysis of both background sources, presented in Appendix <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7app2\">B</a>, we show that their SEDs are well defined at short (HLock01-B) and long wavelengths (HLock01-R), where these two components dominate, respectively. HLock01-B is very bright in the rest-frame UV and optical, but faint (or undetected) in the current VLA and SMA data. On the other hand, HLock01-R shows a very red and obscured counterpart in the rest-frame UV and optical, but it is very bright in the submm. However, to deblend the emission from the two components in the IRAC bands is challenging, given the limitation of the low spatial resolution. The centroids of the bright lensed images A and C seen in the IRAC 3.6 and 4.5 <em>\u03bc</em>m bands are slightly offset (<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />7) with respect to the bright counterparts in the optical and submm, suggesting a contribution of both to the total flux density in IRAC bands. However, the small rest-frame UV spectral slope of HLock01-B, <em>\u03b2</em>\u00a0=\u00a0\u22121.9\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1 (measured from the observed <em>R</em> and <em>I</em> bands, and assuming a simple power law <em>F</em><sub><em>\u03bb</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a0<em>\u03bb</em><sup><em>\u03b2</em></sup>), and the low Balmer/4000 \u00c5 break color (F110W\u2013<em>K</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.15 mag), suggest that the contribution of the LBG in the mid-IR is modest compared with the emission from the SMG. Also, typical LBGs are faint in the mid-IR (<em>S</em><sub>24 <em>\u03bc</em>m</sub>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a020\u201330 <em>\u03bc</em>Jy; Magdis et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib86\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib86\">2010a</a>; Reddy et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib118\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib118\">2012</a>), even those showing a redder UV <em>\u03b2</em> slope (Reddy et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib121\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib121\">2006</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib119\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib119\">2010</a>; Coppin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib31\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib31\">2007</a>; Siana et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib140\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib140\">2008</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib139\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib139\">2009</a>; Magdis et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib87\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib87\">2017</a>), which are on average more massive and show larger infrared luminosities.</p><p>Additionally, in strong gravitational lensing, the finite extend of one or multiple background sources can lead to significant differential magnification, and their intrinsic properties, derived from photometric or spectroscopic diagnostics, can be incorrect if this effect is not taken into account (e.g., Hezaveh et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib61\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib61\">2012</a>; Serjeant <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib136\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib136\">2012</a>). Of particular importance in treating differential magnification are the cases with multiple background sources with significantly different SEDs and positions in the source plane (e.g., the <em>z</em>\u00a0~\u00a02.9 gravitational lensed system analyzed in MacKenzie et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib85\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib85\">2014</a>). To check this effect in HLock01, we use the high S/N and high spatial resolution <em>HST</em>/F110W imaging data to update the lens model already described in Gavazzi et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib50\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib50\">2011</a>). The procedure is detailed in Appendix <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7app3\">C</a>. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f7\">7</a> shows the mean positions and ellipses characterizing the galaxy shapes in the source plane for all wavebands. Stellar emission in the optical/near-IR (LBG) is coincident and slightly offset by 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />42\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />07 in the source plane from the mutually coincident VLA, CO, and dust emission (SMG). We find magnification factors of <em>\u03bc</em>\u00a0=\u00a08.5\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.5 for <em>HST</em> F110W, <em>\u03bc</em>\u00a0=\u00a08.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.3 for GTC <em>g</em> band, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn18.gif\" alt=\"$\\mu ={8.2}_{-0.8}^{+0.6}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mu ={8.2}_{-0.8}^{+0.6}</script></span></span> for VLA, <em>\u03bc</em>\u00a0= 9.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.8 for PdBI CO <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn19.gif\" alt=\"$(J=5\\to 4$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">(J=5\\to 4</script></span></span>), and <em>\u03bc</em>\u00a0=\u00a09.2\u00a0\u00b1 0.5 for the SMA dust continuum. The differential magnification appears to be small, since the bulk of the source emission of the LBG and SMG stands relatively far from the caustics without crossing them (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaaabb7f7\">7</a>), and thus changes of magnification as a function of source plane position vary very little. We thus assume, for simplicity, lensing magnifications of <em>\u03bc</em><sub><em>HST</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a08.5\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.5 and <em>\u03bc</em><sub>SMA</sub>\u00a0=\u00a09.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.5 to be the same in the spectral range in which the LBG and the SMG are well detected, respectively.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaaabb7f7\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaaabb7f7\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f7_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 7.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 7.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7f7_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 7.</strong>\u00a0Source plane reconstruction of HLock01. The posterior mean effective ellipses of the reconstructed components of HLock01-B (LBG) from <em>HST</em> F110W and GTC <em>g</em> band are represented by blue colored ellipses. Pink, yellow, and red colored ellipses represent the effective radius of the reconstructed components of CO, VLA, and dust emission associated with HLock01-R (SMG), respectively. A relative offset of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />42\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />07 is seen between <em>HST</em> F110W and VLA, which corresponds to 3.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.6 kpc.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaaabb7f7\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f7\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaaabb7f7\" href=\"/0004-637X/854/2/151/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaaabb7f7\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>We first used the SED-fitting code <span class=\"small-caps\">Fast</span> (Fitting and Assessment of Synthetic Templates; Kriek et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib76\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib76\">2009</a>) to derive the stellar population properties of HLock01-B. Optical <em>U</em>, <em>g</em>, <em>R</em>, and <em>I</em>, and near-IR F110W and <em>K</em><sub>s</sub> flux measurements were used in this fit (see Appendix <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7app2\">B</a>). We excluded fluxes from IRAC from this fit, given the uncertainties of the contribution of HLock01-B in these bands. However, the 2.2 <em>\u03bc</em>m <em>K</em><sub>s</sub> band corresponds to rest-frame emission at 5600 \u00c5, above the Balmer/4000 \u00c5 break, which is sensitive to the age of the stellar population. We assume stellar population synthesis models of Bruzual &amp; Charlot (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib14\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib14\">2003</a>), the Chabrier (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib25\">2003</a>) IMF, and an exponentially declining star formation history (\u221d<em>e</em><sup>\u2212t/<em>\u03c4</em></sup>). We adopt a grid for the age of the stellar population, ranging from 20 Myr to the maximum age of the universe at <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a02.95, and star formation histories with <em>\u03c4</em> between 0.3 and 10 Gyr, both in steps of 0.1 dex. The attenuation curve of Calzetti et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib18\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib18\">2000</a>) was adopted, and the allowed <em>A</em><sub><em>V</em></sub> range was 0\u20133 mag in steps of 0.05 mag. We also fixed the metallicity to <em>Z</em>/<em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.4, the value measured in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7s3-3\">3.3</a> for the young O and B stars. The best-fit model (<em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup>/<em>N</em><sub>dof</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.6/3) gives an intrinsic (i.e., corrected for the lensing magnification <em>\u03bc</em><sub><em>HST</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a08.5\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.5 and assumed to be the same in the spectral range in which the LBG is well detected) stellar mass log(<em>M</em><sub>*</sub>/<em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>) <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn20.gif\" alt=\"$=\\,{10.1}_{-0.1}^{+0.3}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">=\\,{10.1}_{-0.1}^{+0.3}</script></span></span>, and an attenuation of the stellar light of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn21.gif\" alt=\"${A}_{V}={0.84}_{-0.25}^{+0.12}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{A}_{V}={0.84}_{-0.25}^{+0.12}</script></span></span>, with age log(<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn22.gif\" alt=\"${\\mathrm{age}}_{M}/{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1})\\,={7.3}_{-0.0}^{+0.6}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\mathrm{age}}_{M}/{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1})\\,={7.3}_{-0.0}^{+0.6}</script></span></span>. Errors refer to 68% confidence intervals derived using 500 Monte Carlo simulations. After correction for the lensing magnification, the star formation rate of the best-fit model is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn23.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{SFR}={710}_{-420}^{+180}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{SFR}={710}_{-420}^{+180}</script></span></span> <em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub> yr<sup>\u22121</sup>.</p><p>We further performed a multiband SED fit of HLock01-R using the high-<em>z</em> extension of <span class=\"small-caps\">Magphys</span> (Multi-wavelength Analysis of Galaxy Physical Properties; da Cunha et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib32\">2008</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib33\">2015</a>) to explore its SFR, and stellar and dust mass (<em>M</em><sub>d</sub>). <span class=\"small-caps\">Magphys</span> uses the Bruzual &amp; Charlot (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib14\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib14\">2003</a>) stellar populations with a Chabrier (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib25\">2003</a>) IMF and assumes the attenuation model of Charlot &amp; Fall (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib28\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib28\">2000</a>). We used the flux measurements from 1.1 <em>\u03bc</em>m to radio. In the <em>Spitzer</em>/IRAC bands, we used the difference between the total fluxes (measured in Appendix <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7app2\">B</a>) and the expected flux of HLock01-B from the best-fit SED, as indicated in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaaabb7t6\">6</a>. The best-fit model (reduced <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup>\u00a0=\u00a03.1) gives a lensing corrected (<em>\u03bc</em><sub>SMA</sub>\u00a0=\u00a09.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.5) stellar mass log(<em>M</em><sub>*</sub>/<em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>)<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/854/2/151/Full/apjaaabb7ieqn24.gif\" alt=\"$={11.7}_{-0.1}^{+0.2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">={11.7}_{-0.1}^{+0.2}</script></span></span>, a mass weighted age log(age<sub><em>M</em></sub>/yr)\u00a0=\u00a08.6\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1, and a large attenuation <em>A</em><sub><em>V</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a04.26<sub>\u22120.10</sub><sup>+0.35</sup> mag. We find a dust mass log(<em>M</em><sub>d</sub>/<em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>)\u00a0=8.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1, with a dust temperature <em>T</em><sub>d</sub>\u00a0= (53.6\u00a0\u00b1 0.2) K. The uncertainties are derived from the 16th and 84th percentiles. The best-fit SED also yields an intrinsic total infrared luminosity <em>L</em><sub>IR</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0(1.5\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1)\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a010<sup>13</sup><em>L</em><sub>\u2299</sub>, which is defined as the luminosity from 8 to 1000 <em>\u03bc</em>m in the rest frame. Using a Kennicutt relation (Kennicutt <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib73\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib73\">1998</a>) with a Chabrier IMF (Chabrier <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaaabb7bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjaaabb7bib25\">2003</a>), the total infrared luminosity implies a star formation rate of <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />1500 <em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub> yr<sup>\u22121</sup>. All values were corrected for the lensing magnification derived from the SMA 880 <em>\u03bc</em>m data (<em>\u03bc</em><sub>SMA</sub>\u00a0=9.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.5), which for simplicity, we assume to be the same from the observed near-IR to submm bands for HLock01-R.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaaabb7t6\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table
